{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_017yvi6EK9iE1qg85r3QbT8f","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→//! # The Rust Prelude\n     2→//!\n     3→//! Rust comes with a variety of things in its standard library. However, if\n     4→//! you had to manually import every single thing that you used, it would be\n     5→//! very verbose. But importing a lot of things that a program never uses isn't\n     6→//! good either. A balance needs to be struck.\n     7→//!\n     8→//! The *prelude* is the list of things that Rust automatically imports into\n     9→//! every Rust program. It's kept as small as possible, and is focused on\n    10→//! things, particularly traits, which are used in almost every single Rust\n    11→//! program.\n    12→//!\n    13→//! # Other preludes\n    14→//!\n    15→//! Preludes can be seen as a pattern to make using multiple types more\n    16→//! convenient. As such, you'll find other preludes in the standard library,\n    17→//! such as [`std::io::prelude`]. Various libraries in the Rust ecosystem may\n    18→//! also define their own preludes.\n    19→//!\n    20→//! [`std::io::prelude`]: crate::io::prelude\n    21→//!\n    22→//! The difference between 'the prelude' and these other preludes is that they\n    23→//! are not automatically `use`'d, and must be imported manually. This is still\n    24→//! easier than importing all of their constituent components.\n    25→//!\n    26→//! # Prelude contents\n    27→//!\n    28→//! The items included in the prelude depend on the edition of the crate.\n    29→//! The first version of the prelude is used in Rust 2015 and Rust 2018,\n    30→//! and lives in [`std::prelude::v1`].\n    31→//! [`std::prelude::rust_2015`] and [`std::prelude::rust_2018`] re-export this prelude.\n    32→//! It re-exports the following:\n    33→//!\n    34→//! * <code>[std::marker]::{[Copy], [Send], [Sized], [Sync], [Unpin]}</code>,\n    35→//!   marker traits that indicate fundamental properties of types.\n    36→//! * <code>[std::ops]::{[Fn], [FnMut], [FnOnce]}</code>, and their analogous\n    37→//!   async traits, <code>[std::ops]::{[AsyncFn], [AsyncFnMut], [AsyncFnOnce]}</code>.\n    38→//! * <code>[std::ops]::[Drop]</code>, for implementing destructors.\n    39→//! * <code>[std::mem]::[drop]</code>, a convenience function for explicitly\n    40→//!   dropping a value.\n    41→//! * <code>[std::mem]::{[size_of], [size_of_val]}</code>, to get the size of\n    42→//!   a type or value.\n    43→//! * <code>[std::mem]::{[align_of], [align_of_val]}</code>, to get the\n    44→//!   alignment of a type or value.\n    45→//! * <code>[std::boxed]::[Box]</code>, a way to allocate values on the heap.\n    46→//! * <code>[std::borrow]::[ToOwned]</code>, the conversion trait that defines\n    47→//!   [`to_owned`], the generic method for creating an owned type from a\n    48→//!   borrowed type.\n    49→//! * <code>[std::clone]::[Clone]</code>, the ubiquitous trait that defines\n    50→//!   [`clone`][Clone::clone], the method for producing a copy of a value.\n    51→//! * <code>[std::cmp]::{[PartialEq], [PartialOrd], [Eq], [Ord]}</code>, the\n    52→//!   comparison traits, which implement the comparison operators and are often\n    53→//!   seen in trait bounds.\n    54→//! * <code>[std::convert]::{[AsRef], [AsMut], [Into], [From]}</code>, generic\n    55→//!   conversions, used by savvy API authors to create overloaded methods.\n    56→//! * <code>[std::default]::[Default]</code>, types that have default values.\n    57→//! * <code>[std::iter]::{[Iterator], [Extend], [IntoIterator], [DoubleEndedIterator], [ExactSizeIterator]}</code>,\n    58→//!   iterators of various\n    59→//!   kinds.\n    60→//! * <code>[std::option]::[Option]::{[self][Option], [Some], [None]}</code>, a\n    61→//!   type which expresses the presence or absence of a value. This type is so\n    62→//!   commonly used, its variants are also exported.\n    63→//! * <code>[std::result]::[Result]::{[self][Result], [Ok], [Err]}</code>, a type\n    64→//!   for functions that may succeed or fail. Like [`Option`], its variants are\n    65→//!   exported as well.\n    66→//! * <code>[std::string]::{[String], [ToString]}</code>, heap-allocated strings.\n    67→//! * <code>[std::vec]::[Vec]</code>, a growable, heap-allocated vector.\n    68→//!\n    69→//! The prelude used in Rust 2021, [`std::prelude::rust_2021`], includes all of the above,\n    70→//! and in addition re-exports:\n    71→//!\n    72→//! * <code>[std::convert]::{[TryFrom], [TryInto]}</code>.\n    73→//! * <code>[std::iter]::[FromIterator]</code>.\n    74→//!\n    75→//! The prelude used in Rust 2024, [`std::prelude::rust_2024`], includes all of the above,\n    76→//! and in addition re-exports:\n    77→//!\n    78→//! * <code>[std::future]::{[Future], [IntoFuture]}</code>.\n    79→//!\n    80→//! [std::borrow]: crate::borrow\n    81→//! [std::boxed]: crate::boxed\n    82→//! [std::clone]: crate::clone\n    83→//! [std::cmp]: crate::cmp\n    84→//! [std::convert]: crate::convert\n    85→//! [std::default]: crate::default\n    86→//! [std::future]: crate::future\n    87→//! [std::iter]: crate::iter\n    88→//! [std::marker]: crate::marker\n    89→//! [std::mem]: crate::mem\n    90→//! [std::ops]: crate::ops\n    91→//! [std::option]: crate::option\n    92→//! [`std::prelude::v1`]: v1\n    93→//! [`std::prelude::rust_2015`]: rust_2015\n    94→//! Rust comes with a variety of things in its standard library. However, if\n//! you had to manually import every single thing that you used, it would be\n//! very verbose. But importing a lot of things that a program never uses isn't\n//! good either. A balance needs to be struck.\n//!\n//! The *prelude* is the list of things that Rust automatically imports into\n//! every Rust program. It's kept as small as possible, and is focused on\n//! things, particularly traits, which are used in almost every single Rust\n//! program.\n//!\n//! # Other preludes\n//!\n//! Preludes can be seen as a pattern to make using multiple types more\n//! convenient. As such, you'll find other preludes in the standard library,\n//! such as [`std::io::prelude`]. Various libraries in the Rust ecosystem may\n//! also define their own preludes.\n//!\n//! [`std::io::prelude`]: crate::io::prelude\n//!\n//! The difference between 'the prelude' and these other preludes is that they\n//! are not automatically `use`'d, and must be imported manually. This is still\n//! easier than importing all of their constituent components.\n//!\n//! # Prelude contents\n//!\n//! The items included in the prelude depend on the edition of the crate.\n//! The first version of the prelude is used in Rust 2015 and Rust 2018,\n//! and lives in [`std::prelude::v1`].\n//! [`std::prelude::rust_2015`] and [`std::prelude::rust_2018`] re-export this prelude.\n//! It re-exports the following:\n//!\n//! * <code>[std::marker]::{[Copy], [Send], [Sized], [Sync], [Unpin]}</code>,\n//!   marker traits that indicate fundamental properties of types.\n//! * <code>[std::ops]::{[Fn], [FnMut], [FnOnce]}</code>, and their analogous\n//!   async traits, <code>[std::ops]::{[AsyncFn], [AsyncFnMut], [AsyncFnOnce]}</code>.\n//! * <code>[std::ops]::[Drop]</code>, for implementing destructors.\n//! * <code>[std::mem]::[drop]</code>, a convenience function for explicitly\n//!   dropping a value.\n//! * <code>[std::mem]::{[size_of], [size_of_val]}</code>, to get the size of\n//!   a type or value.\n//! * <code>[std::mem]::{[align_of], [align_of_val]}</code>, to get the\n//!   alignment of a type or value.\n//! * <code>[std::boxed]::[Box]</code>, a way to allocate values on the heap.\n//! * <code>[std::borrow]::[ToOwned]</code>, the conversion trait that defines\n//!   [`to_owned`], the generic method for creating an owned type from a\n//!   borrowed type.\n//! * <code>[std::clone]::[Clone]</code>, the ubiquitous trait that defines\n//!   [`clone`][Clone::clone], the method for producing a copy of a value.\n//! * <code>[std::cmp]::{[PartialEq], [PartialOrd], [Eq], [Ord]}</code>, the\n//!   comparison traits, which implement the comparison operators and are often\n//!   seen in trait bounds.\n//! * <code>[std::convert]::{[AsRef], [AsMut], [Into], [From]}</code>, generic\n//!   conversions, used by savvy API authors to create overloaded methods.\n//! * <code>[std::default]::[Default]</code>, types that have default values.\n//! * <code>[std::iter]::{[Iterator], [Extend], [IntoIterator], [DoubleEndedIterator], [ExactSizeIterator]}</code>,\n//!   iterators of various\n//!   kinds.\n//! * <code>[std::option]::[Option]::{[self][Option], [Some], [None]}</code>, a\n//!   type which expresses the presence or absence of a value. This type is so\n//!   commonly used, its variants are also exported.\n//! * <code>[std::result]::[Result]::{[self][Result], [Ok], [Err]}</code>, a type\n//!   for functions that may succeed or fail. Like [`Option`], its variants are\n//!   exported as well.\n//! * <code>[std::string]::{[String], [ToString]}</code>, heap-allocated strings.\n//! * <code>[std::vec]::[Vec]</code>, a growable, heap-allocated vector.\n//!\n//! The prelude used in Rust 2021, [`std::prelude::rust_2021`], includes all of the above,\n//! and in addition re-exports:\n//!\n//! * <code>[std::convert]::{[TryFrom], [TryInto]}</code>.\n//! * <code>[std::iter]::[FromIterator]</code>.\n//!\n//! The prelude used in Rust 2024, [`std::prelude::rust_2024`], includes all of the above,\n//! and in addition re-exports:\n//!\n//! * <code>[std::future]::{[Future], [IntoFuture]}</code>.\n//!\n//! [std::borrow]: crate::borrow\n//! [std::boxed]: crate::boxed\n//! [std::clone]: crate::clone\n//! [std::cmp]: crate::cmp\n//! [std::convert]: crate::convert\n//! [std::default]: crate::default\n//! [std::future]: crate::future\n//! [std::iter]: crate::iter\n//! [std::marker]: crate::marker\n//! [std::mem]: crate::mem\n//! [std::ops]: crate::ops\n//! [std::option]: crate::option\n//! \"The Rust edition 2018 to 2021 import path migration is implemented across multiple components of the rust-lang/rust repository:\\n\\n**Prelude Structure (library/core/src/prelude/mod.rs and library/std/src/prelude/mod.rs):**\\nBoth core and std libraries define edition-specific prelude modules (rust_2015, rust_2018, rust_2021, rust_2024). The core prelude (library/core/src/prelude/v1.rs) serves as the base for all editions. In edition 2021, the core prelude adds FromIterator and conversion traits (TryFrom, TryInto) via the rust_2021 module. The std prelude (library/std/src/prelude/v1.rs) re-exports these items with edition-specific modules that import from the core prelude.\\n\\n**Edition-Based Macro and Import Injection (compiler/rustc_builtin_macros/src/standard_library_imports.rs):**\\nThis file implements the inject() function that automatically inserts a #[macro_use] extern crate declaration and a prelude glob import into every crate. The crucial edition-specific behavior is:\\n- Edition 2015 and earlier: Uses call_site span for identifiers (imports from root)\\n- Edition 2018 and later: Uses def_site span for identifiers (uniform paths)\\n- Edition selection: Lines 55-61 select the appropriate prelude module (rust_2015, rust_2018, rust_2021, rust_2024) based on the crate's edition\\n\\n**Macro_use and Prelude_import Attribute Handling (compiler/rustc_resolve/src/build_reduced_graph.rs):**\\nThis file handles the resolution of macro_use and prelude_import attributes:\\n- process_macro_use_imports(): Processes #[macro_use] attributes on extern crate and mod items, making macros available in the macro_use_prelude scope\\n- add_macro_use_binding(): Adds macro bindings to the macro_use_prelude map\\n- contains_macro_use(): Checks for #[macro_use] attributes\\nThese functions are edition-aware as they're invoked for all crates regardless of edition, but the prelude_import attribute specifically marks the stdlib prelude imports.\\n\\n**Prelude Edition Collision Detection (compiler/rustc_hir_typeck/src/method/prelude_edition_lints.rs):**\\nThis file implements lint_edition_dependent_dot_call() and lint_fully_qualified_call_from_2018() to detect when methods from prelude additions will become ambiguous:\\n- Edition 2021 additions (TryFrom, TryInto, FromIterator)\\n- Edition 2024 additions (Future::poll, IntoFuture::into_future)\\nUses span.at_least_rust_2021() and span.at_least_rust_2024() to determine applicability.\\n\\n**Edition Definition and Helpers (compiler/rustc_span/src/edition.rs):**\\nDefines the Edition enum (Edition2015, Edition2018, Edition2021, Edition2024, EditionFuture) and provides methods like at_least_rust_2021() and at_least_rust_2024() to check edition capabilities.\\n\\n**Resolver Prelude and Macro Scope Management (compiler/rustc_resolve/src/lib.rs):**\\nThe Resolver struct maintains:\\n- macro_use_prelude: FxIndexMap containing macros injected via #[macro_use]\\n- no_implicit_prelude: bool flag for #[no_implicit_prelude] attribute\\n- Scope::MacroUsePrelude and Scope::StdLibPrelude for name resolution\\nThese enable separate resolution paths for macros injected via #[macro_use] versus those from the standard prelude.\\n\\n**Supporting Infrastructure:**\\n- compiler/rustc_builtin_macros/src/edition_panic.rs: Implements edition-specific panic! macro behavior\\n- compiler/rustc_feature/src/builtin_attrs.rs: Defines the prelude_import attribute (line 1352-1353)\\n- compiler/rustc_feature/src/unstable.rs: Declares prelude_import as an internal unstable feature\\n- compiler/rustc_lint_defs/src/builtin.rs: Defines RUST_2021_PRELUDE_COLLISIONS and RUST_2024_PRELUDE_COLLISIONS lints\\n- compiler/rustc_resolve/src/macros.rs: Macro resolution logic that respects edition-aware scope rules\\n- compiler/rustc_resolve/src/imports.rs: Import resolution with edition-aware path handling\\n\\nThe key architectural insight is that Rust 2018 and 2021 differ in how the standard library prelude is injected and resolved. Edition 2018 introduced uniform paths (no implicit crate root), while edition 2021 added new items to the prelude that can cause name collisions. This migration required changes at both the library level (adding separate prelude modules per edition) and the compiler level (edition-aware prelude injection and collision detection).\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":13,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4663,"cache_read_input_tokens":54514,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4663},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"466f4766-d0a0-4e22-80e5-a3a2721b71da","uuid":"fed3f7d7-0f24-4f33-9bda-9b13b38bea8d"}
